China Accounting Society Held Board Meeting in Shanghai Yesterday Morning 172

The China Accounting Society is the only academic organization in the country dedicated to the study of accounting. It was initiated by accounting experts such as Lin Jinyu, Zhao Dihua, Wen Yiyou, Yong Jiayuan, Wu Shirui, Ren Yingzhong, Pan Xulun, and Xu Yongzuo, and was officially established at the inaugural meeting held in Nanjing on November 18, 1934. The first and second board meetings discussed and decided on a five-point plan for the development of the society: (1) hold accounting academic discussion meetings, (2) hold academic lecture meetings, (3) establish an accounting library, (4) run accounting schools, and (5) compile and translate accounting books and newspapers, to be implemented gradually. It is said that the society's membership qualifications are very strict. In addition to being introduced by two or more existing members, applicants must also submit their own works or papers, which are reviewed by the board of directors before they can become official members. It is anticipated that the study and promotion of accounting will progress rapidly in our country through the society's research and promotion. It is now learned that the society held its third board meeting at 10 AM yesterday (January 20) at Xu Yongzuo's accounting firm on Avenue Edward VII in this city. The meeting was attended by nine directors: Zhao Dihua, Wen Yiyou, Wei Tingsheng (represented by Wen), Yong Jiayuan, Wu Shirui, Ren Yingzhong, Lin Jinyu (represented by Zhao), Pan Xulun, and Xu Yongzuo. Director Zhao Dihua presided over the meeting, and society member Yang Zezhang served as the recorder. After the meeting was convened, the following matters were discussed: (1) Proposal to establish an affiliated accounting training school. It was resolved: 1. Appoint Director Wu Shirui as the principal and start preparations. 2. Determine the budget for the first semester. If the tuition fees are insufficient, the board of directors will make up the difference. 3. Divide the school into high and elementary levels. The elementary level will adopt a school year system, and the high level will adopt a course-based system. (2) Proposal by Li Yiren, accounting director of the Xijing Daily, to introduce colleagues from the Xijing Accounting Office to join the society and to organize a Xijing branch. It was resolved: Please complete the membership procedures first. (3) Proposal by Lu Shanzhi and others to submit works and papers and request to join the society. It was resolved: Approved. (4) Proposal for the date and location of the fourth board meeting. It was resolved: To be held in Wuxi on the first Sunday of April. The meeting adjourned at 12:30 PM.

Record of the Second General Meeting of the Banking Association 173

The Shanghai Banking Association held its second general meeting at 5:00 PM on January 19th of this year in the conference hall of the Bankers' Association at No. 59 Hong Kong Road in this city. Mr. Zhu Boquan, the chairman of the association, served as the chairman of the meeting. After the formal opening ceremony, the chairman delivered an opening speech. The main points of the opening speech can be divided into three aspects: (1) a description of the origins of the Banking Association; (2) the contributions of the British Bankers' Association to the British banking industry; and (3) the hope that all members would utilize the organization of the Banking Association to make academic efforts. Subsequently, Mr. Mao Xiaxuan, the representative of the City Party Headquarters, delivered a speech. The main points of Mr. Mao's speech were to express the hope that the Banking Association would conduct substantial research on banking operations, and find ways to promote rural investment and establish various industries, so that the national banks would move towards a proper path. Afterwards, Dr. Ma Yinchu delivered a lecture on the silver issue. Dr. Ma discussed extensively the strategies of general economists to remedy the outflow of silver, with the following main points: 1. Measures to restrict import trade. China's annual trade deficit is very large, approximately 770 million yuan in 1933 and approximately 550 million yuan in 1934. To prohibit the export of silver, it is necessary to first find a solution to the trade deficit problem. Therefore, restricting import trade is a good measure, but there are two difficulties in implementation. Firstly, to restrict import trade, it is necessary to first investigate domestic needs and domestic production. However, China lacks reliable statistical materials, making this step of work quite difficult. Secondly, there are many foreign exporting merchants, and to restrict their import volume, it is impossible to directly negotiate with each merchant. It is necessary to entrust the governments of those countries to handle the matter. Once this agreement is signed, it is quite difficult to cancel. Our country has been constrained by tariff agreements in the past, and now making trade agreements, this kind of policy, I am afraid, will be difficult to obtain public support. 2. Centralized and controlled issuance measures. Concentrating the existing silver and having a central institution responsible for issuance, and then adding controlled issuance measures. The implementation of this method can both restrain import trade and protect domestic silver. However, the selection of this central institution is quite difficult. However, our country must eventually adopt a centralized issuance system. If the difficulties can be overcome, then using centralized and controlled issuance to restrain import trade and protect domestic silver may not be a good policy. 3. Measures to lower the exchange rate. Various countries have used methods of lowering their exchange rates to lower the exchange rate and encourage export trade. When they adopted this method, they had considerable backgrounds. For example, when US President Roosevelt adopted the policy of lowering the exchange rate, it was because the general farmers in the United States were debtors. After the value of the US currency was lowered, prices increased, making it easier for debtors to repay their debts. If our country adopts this method, it will be difficult to gain national sympathy because raising prices will make the general public feel even more difficult in their lives. 4. Trade associations of various industries automatically restrict the purchase of foreign goods. The nature of this method is the same as restricting trade, but it is not restricted by the government, but rather each industry association automatically stipulates the amount of foreign goods purchased by the corresponding industry. After Dr. Ma's lecture, a dinner was held. At the same time, Secretary Tang Boyuan reported on the general situation of the association's affairs in 1934, announced the results of the essay competition of the general meeting, and announced the results of the election of new directors. The meeting adjourned at 9:00 PM.

As a result, they arrested a suspect named Qian Chunzhao, a native of Yancheng, at the Laohuzao teahouse at No. 82 Jumen Road, and took him to the station along with the other suspect, preparing a document and the confession to transfer them to the Ximen Branch for interrogation. Six pawn tickets, ninety-three copper coins, and four firecrackers were found on Yang. It is reported that after learning of the incident, the French police also dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to arrest the suspects. After chasing them to the Chinese-controlled area, the police officers and members of the Self-Defense Corps assisted in apprehending the bandits. Therefore, Deputy Detective Sui Wenzhi, No. 31, went to the Ximen Branch to request the Ximen Branch Chief Li to bring them back for questioning. After Chief Li requested instructions from the General Bureau, he was allowed to hand over the two suspects, Yang and Qian, to the officers to take to the French authorities for legal proceedings.

Wang Xiaotong's New Book "Essentials of Commercial Law" 178

Wang Xiaotong, an expert in commercial law, has previously authored the New Era Legal Series "Negotiable Instruments Law" and "Company Law" (published by Commercial Press), "On Chinese Company Law", "On Chinese Maritime Law", "On Chinese Insurance Law" and "General Outline of Chinese Commercial Law" (published by World Press), the Huatong Legal Series "Maritime Law" (published by Huatong Press), "On Insurance Law", "General Discussions on Commercial Law" (published by Huiwentang Press), "Essentials of Negotiable Instruments Law" and "Essentials of Company Law" (published by Shanghai Legal Books Publishing House). These books have long been popular, and many universities in China have adopted them as textbooks. Recently, he has based his experience of teaching commercial law for twenty years and written a book entitled "Essentials of Commercial Law," which was published by the Commercial Press a month ago (now published). The contents of the book are divided into five sections: introduction, company, negotiable instruments, maritime affairs, and insurance, totaling 150,000 words. The material is novel, and the writing is concise. At the end of the book, there are appendices including the Proposal for a Unified Civil and Commercial Code, the Proposal for Uniformity of Civil and Commercial Law, the Review Report, the Draft Principles of Company Law, the General Explanatory Book, the Preliminary Investigation Report on Company Law, the Explanatory Book of the Draft Negotiable Instruments Law, and the Principles of Negotiable Instruments Law for readers' reference. It is truly a guide for those who study commercial law.

News of Calligraphy and Painting 185

▲ Zhu Shaoyi Writes Characters to Help Disaster Relief Regarding the visit of the famous painter Zhu Shaoyi to Shanghai, which was recorded in this newspaper on the 13th, Zhu is a native of Luoshan County, Henan Province, born in the year Gui Si during the reign of Emperor Guangxu in the late Qing Dynasty. He studied poetry and books in his youth and traveled to Ban'shui in his adulthood. In the first year of the Republic of China, he participated in the revolution in Wuhan and then studied at the Russian Language Society of the Dongqing Railway in Heilongjiang. After completing his studies, he studied at the Moscow Academy of Fine Arts in Russia. He returned to China in five years due to the outbreak of the European War. In six years, he entered politics in Guangdong under General Zhu Yuqiao for seven or eight years. He traveled to the Nanyang Islands and major commercial ports overseas, holding the ambition to travel around the world. Last year, he returned to China. In view of the increasingly difficult national affairs, he studied Taoism under the guidance of Mr. Song Ziyi to learn meditation, emptiness, and static work, and also wrote Buddhist characters of three to five feet, cultivating Taoism and writing, advancing in both for decades. In the twentieth year of the Republic of China, he asked for disaster relief in Shanghai to distribute to the Yu people who were living in Taihu Lake in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. In the years of Nianyi and Nianer, he traveled in Suzhou and Hangzhou, helping disaster relief with calligraphy. In the year of Niansan, he wrote characters to help disaster relief in the border areas of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui. In the same year, he participated in the Henan Celebrity Calligraphy and Painting Exhibition on Double Tenth Day. He arrived in Shanghai in January of this year. He has received sponsorship from famous celebrities and scholars in Shanghai, and he is ashamed that he cannot repay them. He is temporarily residing at Renji Lane 27, Ximen Road, French Concession, to cultivate stillness. When the work is completed, he will write characters to help disaster relief.

▲ Wen Wu Calligraphy and Painting Exhibition The Wen Kegang and Wu Gonghu Charity Calligraphy and Painting Exhibition opened today at the Hueshe on Guizhou Road. The two artists have each produced masterpieces, totaling more than two hundred pieces, a dazzling array of beauty.

Letter to the Editor 188

Dear Editor, Upon reading the "Buddhism Groups Cast Giant Far East Bell" news item in the local news column of yesterday's (19th) issue of your newspaper, there are two points that do not conform to the facts: (1) The initiating groups are the China Buddhist Association, the Shanghai Buddhist Association, the Jiuhua Buddhist Association, the Buddhist Pure Karma Society, the World Buddhist Laymen's Society, and the Buddhist Book Bureau. Yesterday's newspaper mistakenly listed the "Buddhist Lianhua Society" as one of the initiating groups and omitted the Jiuhua Buddhist Association. (2) Yesterday's newspaper stated that "the bell is currently being manufactured by Shen Yuanji Foundry in Pudong," which is also not a fact. It is verified that the model bell that has been cast and displayed was made by the foundry. As for which foundry will be commissioned to officially cast the giant bell in the future, it has not yet been determined. It may be necessary to hold a bidding process to decide, in order to be fair and just. Therefore, we are sending this letter to request a correction and hope that you will publish this letter in the Letter to the Editor column of your newspaper to make a correction. We would be extremely grateful. Sincerely, The Preparatory Office for the Construction of the Youming Bell of Jiuhua Mountain, January 20.

Urgent

Basic Principles of the Five-Power Constitution by Zhang Yuanruo 189

Public law scholar Zhang Yuanruo, at the invitation of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education, delivered a broadcast lecture at the Shanghai Sino-Western Radio Station, entitled "Basic Principles of the Five-Power Constitution." The original manuscript is recorded below:

I. Introduction

Today, at the invitation of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education, I am here to deliver a broadcast lecture entitled "The Five-Power Constitution." This topic was predetermined by the Bureau of Education. Due to time constraints, I am unable to elaborate in detail. I will supplement any omissions with a special article.

There is no law that lasts forever, nor is there a perfect system. Han Fei said, "If the law changes with the times, it will be well-governed; if the governance suits the world, it will be meritorious." (Han Fei's "Heart and Measure" chapter). Since the founding of the Republic of China, although we have tried the good systems of various countries in the world, we have rarely achieved long-term stability and effective governance. Therefore, when discussing the central political system today, we must not seek extravagant hopes that are divorced from reality, but only seek to establish laws and execute orders, achieving "suitability and merit."

II. Basic Principles of the Five-Power Constitution

Politics, by its nature, cannot completely escape the relationship of strength and weakness. Regardless of the political system, its practical application cannot deviate from this principle. French jurist L. Duguit said that the origin of the state lies in the existence of strong and weak humans (Duguit has a separate annotation on the meaning of "strong," see his work "Traite de Droit Constitutionnel"). Haller also argued that the origin of the state is due to force. Duguit and Haller are both famous European scholars whose writings are followed by scholars. Haller's research on the origin of the state took nearly a decade. Their views have inherent truth. Therefore, modern political revolutions have fundamentally different characteristics from the French Revolution. This includes the improvement of parliamentary autocracy and the expansion of administrative power (see my book "Modern Constitutionalism," published by Zhonghua Book Company). The expansion of administrative power is not the "dictatorship" feared by the general public, but is precisely sufficient to "remedy dictatorship" and "prevent dictatorship" (see M. Dendiaq, "Les renforcement des pouvoirs de L'Etat dans la democratie porlementire," Paris, 1932). (Regarding this point, I have elaborated further in my lecture at Fudan University on "Democracy and Dictatorship." I welcome further correction from experts). This is the first basic principle that constitution-makers should confirm today.

Dr. Sun Yat-sen admired the American presidential system most. His highest ideal for the Five-Power Constitution was to realize an "omnipotent" government, enabling the state's administrative power to develop independently. Therefore, Dr. Sun's Three Principles of the People did not inherit the old notions of "natural human rights" and "liberalism," but instead created the theory of "separation of powers and abilities," so that political power and governing power each have their scope and do not infringe upon each other. This is the second basic principle that constitution-makers should confirm today.

III. Understanding That Researchers of Chinese Constitution Should Have

Following the aforementioned principles, those who study the current draft constitution of China should have the following three understandings:

(1) The central political system in today's draft constitution should not continue to follow the established patterns of general constitutional states, blindly believing in the old theory of checks and balances of traditional governing power. The essence of the Five-Power Constitution lies not only in formally increasing three powers to five powers, but also in improving the efficiency of the government's governing power in its application. The principle of checks and balances in the Five-Power Constitution lies in the checks and balances between political power and governing power, and between the rights of the people and the power of the government, not in the mutual restraint of the government's governing power, which would prevent the government from exerting its effectiveness. This is the first understanding that researchers of the Chinese constitution should have today.

(2) Considering that the administrative departments of various countries are only subject to the constraints of the legislative department, there are already drawbacks of inefficiency. Now that our country advocates the so-called "capable government," the Executive Yuan seems to be subject to multiple restrictions from the Legislative Yuan, the Control Yuan, the National Assembly, and the National Committee. Otherwise, it would be even more intensified than the traditional parliamentary system. The theory of checks and balances of governing power originated with Montesquieu. Montesquieu's theory claims to be objective, stating that it is based on British political experience. The strength of British politics lies in the separation of powers and mutual restraint. However, British constitutional scholar Walter Bagehot strongly opposed Montesquieu's theory, stating that the advantage of British politics lies precisely in the harmonious cooperation between parliament and the executive, not in mutual opposition and separation. It can be seen that the checks and balances of governing power are inherently flawed. Moreover, the parliamentary system was originally intended to restrict monarchical power, but the current administrative leaders are all elected by the people. Mutual checks and balances between powers from the same source are also lacking in legal justification. Even from the perspective of modern practical political experience, not only has the arrogance and autocracy of parliaments in various countries been deeply resented by politicians, but also due to the corruption and weakness of parliamentarians, the prestige of parliament has declined. Even James Bryce, who praised representative politics, wrote books criticizing the darkness of parliamentary politics (see my book "Modern Political Overview"). Therefore, the recent principle of political reform tends to strengthen executive power. This is the second understanding that researchers of the Chinese constitution should have today.

(3) Furthermore, the Legislative Yuan under the Five-Power Constitution is fundamentally different in nature from the parliaments of various countries. The Legislative Yuan in our country is a "capable" governing power organ, not a political power organ. Therefore, we must first distinguish between governing power and political power, and the power of the Legislative Yuan cannot infringe upon the functions of the National Assembly. Moreover, the new constitutions of various countries after the war have greatly restricted the legislative power of parliaments, on the one hand, subject to the restrictions of the people's rights, and on the other hand, subject to the restrictions of the president's legislative power. This can be seen from the constitutions of Poland, Czechoslovakia, Finland, Germany, Lithuania, Latvia, and Yugoslavia. Therefore, on the one hand, our constitution should strive to increase administrative power, and on the other hand, it should strive to adjust the relationship between executive and legislative powers. This is the third understanding that researchers of the Chinese constitution should have today. Otherwise, the future operation of the political machinery will inevitably present a state of contradiction and difficulty, and it will be difficult to achieve "the law is established and the orders are carried out" and "suitability and merit." I ask my fellow countrymen for their opinions.

Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise 193

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter 8: Remote Place, Unassuming Official, Strong-Willed Order; Grand Hall, Lavish Feast, Outside, a Pitiful Wretch

Zhiqian pushed back with both hands, saying, "I really don't deserve it. Think about it, Mr. Zhang and he are from the same hometown, so it wouldn't be appropriate for them to receive his things for free. I've never even met him, so how can I accept these valuable items worth thirty or forty dollars?" Zhang Jiefu smiled and said, "If Mr. Cheng feels that he must express his gratitude after accepting them, then just give me the credit. As for him giving them to me, I will naturally repay him. Mr. Cheng doesn't need to worry about it." Zhiqian clasped his fists and smiled, "It's still not appropriate to accept them." Zhang Jiefu placed both hands on the edge of the table, made an extremely difficult expression, and looked at Yuqi, saying, "Mr. Cheng really doesn't want to accept them, there's nothing I can do, but I'll lose too much face. Mr. Li Shilian and I are both new acquaintances of Mr. Cheng. Shilian often comes to Mr. Cheng's house to sit, and even invites Mr. Cheng to dinner. Now, when he comes to my place, I didn't expect that even if I sent something to Mr. Cheng, Mr. Cheng wouldn't appreciate it." Zhiqian couldn't help but chuckle and said, "Brother, what virtues and abilities do I possess that I deserve such kindness from Mr. Zhang? I really don't deserve it. Since you've said so, I'll accept it for now, and when Mr. Zhang needs something, I'll return the favor." Zhang Jiefu smiled when he heard that he was willing to accept it, then cupped his hands and said, "Brother doesn't need anything. If you immediately think about returning the favor after giving something to a friend, then this person is too lacking in self-respect. Where can you find a confidant?" Cheng Zhiqian saw that he was so diligent in giving gifts, there must be something he was asking for, so he would see what it was. If it was a small matter, he would agree, saving him from constantly pestering him. If it was a difficult matter, then he could honestly refuse and say that it was impossible to do. So, he invited him to sit opposite him and offered him tea and cigarettes. Zhang Jiefu first made some small talk, and then talked about the matter of getting a job in the province. (117)

About Phlegm 194

— By Zhao Yu

Westerners and Americans mostly use their own prepared handkerchiefs to wrap their own spit and blown snot, and take them back as recycled goods, not willing to give away a single drop to someone else's house or on the road.

When Japanese people encounter snot and saliva, they mostly use their own prepared paper called "kaimi" to wrap them into small paper balls, throw them into paper scrap boxes, and give them to public servants (garbage collectors) as souvenirs.

Chinese people, if they have snot and saliva, can make any place a display venue for their products (snot and phlegm), regardless of whether people welcome it or not? Whether they want to see it or not? They take no responsibility at all.

From the above, we can obtain the following formula:——

Westerners (handkerchief wrapped) || Japanese (paper wrapped) || Chinese (display anywhere)

The digestion of Westerners' snot and saliva: is digested by clean water and transferred to the sewer.

The digestion of Japanese snot and saliva: is at the crematorium, or the sewer.

The digestion of Chinese snot and saliva: is sun-dried and dispersed in the air.

From this, we can draw a conclusion: that Westerners have relatively fewer infectious diseases.

According to his statistics, the most common infectious diseases among Japanese people are parasitic diseases and tuberculosis.

The most common infectious diseases among Chinese people are scarlet fever, cholera, leprosy, parasitic diseases, and tuberculosis.

Watching the Waterfall at Mount Lao 195

— By Dai Yuren

The weather this winter is warm, and no snowflakes have been seen in Shanghai and Qingdao. Mount Lao, about ninety li away from Qingdao City, is already covered in white snow. At that time, I was temporarily detained in Qingdao due to business. I heard that the snow scene and waterfalls of Mount Lao were quite spectacular, so I hurriedly hired a car to visit. After driving for half an hour, I saw a silver Mount Lao in the distance. After passing the Tanyue Bridge and the Fairy Pagoda, I arrived at the guardhouse in about an hour (the foot of Mount Lao). In the past, when the Germans ruled Qingdao, they set up a police station here, and the old name is still used. The car could have climbed the mountain, passing Liushu Terrace and Laocun Village, and reaching Beijiushui and other places. However, because the mountain slope was covered with slippery snow, it could not go up or down, so it stopped here. So I hired a mountain sedan and went up. First, I had lunch at the Laocun Hotel on Liushu Terrace. The windows were bright and the tables were clean. There were several plates of Western food, which were clean and tasty. Moreover, it was located halfway up the mountain, with elegant equipment. It was very suitable for escaping the summer heat here. After the meal, I took the sedan again, passed Laocun Village and arrived at Beijiushui. The sound of the spring was gurgling, and there were many shallow beaches, similar to the Nine Streams and Eighteen Gullies of West Lake in Hangzhou, but quieter. Further ahead, the cliffs and strange rocks were extremely beautiful and majestic. The higher I went, the deeper the snow accumulated. At this point, it was already five or six inches deep. The road was even more slippery. I tried to get off the sedan and walk, but stopped after a few steps. The sedan carriers, on the other hand, strode forward as if nothing was wrong. After passing several stone steps, I finally reached the waterfall. The sound was like the tide, cascading down in three folds and converging into a pool. The water was clear and bottomless. The stone walls arched around it, and the words "Chaoyin Waterfall" were engraved in high places by Ye Gongchuo. The climate in the mountains was cold. I tried to climb the stone steps and looked at the white snow on the mountain peak from afar, and listened to the sound of the waterfall. I felt the cold air even more chilling and oppressive. I planned to go further to the top of the mountain, but the carriers said that the snow was more than a foot deep, the road was difficult to identify, and it was impossible to go. So I returned by the original route. At five o'clock, I boarded the China Merchants Bureau's Haiheng Wheel, left Qingdao and returned to Shanghai. The wheel is one of the four new wheels, with fast speed and complete equipment, and is the most complete of our country's sea wheels. Moreover, all the service equipment is in line with the tastes of the people of the country. People of the country often like to take foreign wheels. Now they can change to Chinese ships to show their patriotism, so I especially recommend it. (Reward for Refusal)

On the Wuxi-Changzhou Road 196

— By Guocheng

This is my first time walking this Wuxi-Changzhou road. For two years, I've been running from the old capital to the south, wandering along the banks of the Yangtze River all day long. The whip of life won't let me stop for a moment. My exhausted body carries endless time. One day passes, and then another. I haven't even lived in Shanghai for a month, but I have to throw myself onto this road.

The telephone poles fly past the window one after another, accompanied by two or three scattered withered trees. The fields are covered with sparse, withered wheat seedlings, and the rotten leaves of rapeseed are spread out like broken umbrellas. Several thin little goats are tied to the roadside, searching for a few wild grasses left over from winter. Piles of dilapidated peasant huts flash by from time to time—a scene of desolation and decline. The scene of ugliness and brokenness can't help but make people think that the countryside is bankrupt! No matter what, it doesn't seem to be arranged according to my imagination at all. What else is there to say?

Let those young masters from bustling cities who are seeing the rural scenery for the first time write lyrical poems praising the beauty of the countryside. But for a person who wanders around all year round, approaching these so-called "poetic" scenes almost every day, I may not have the energy to get excited.

The long-distance bus is always shivering as if it has a cold, shaking and shaking. The road is bumpy and full of obstacles, but it never stops, rushing towards its destination, finally carrying us to Jiangyin Station, the end point.

Rickshaw pullers rushed to the station like a tide, the noise and roar of people vying for luggage and haggling over prices. This is a picture of the struggle for life.

"If you want to live, you have to fight"! To this day, I cannot deny this sentence.

The Dignity of the City 197

— By Yin Juan

The Sugary Quality of People's Hearts 198

— By Shen Shou Ruo

A heart made of iron and stone is just a figure of speech, after all, it belongs to the realm of ideals.

The facts tell us that people's hearts are close to being made of sugar. The empirical proof is: Sweet love, reaching a high degree of heat, no matter which side's heart is, is always soft and obedient; when love suddenly cools, the hearts begin to harden each other, often forgetting the old days of affection, and each going to extremes! Isn't this the same as the phenomenon of things made of sugar, which are soft when heated and hard when cold?

Therefore, I think: the terms of endearment between men and women in society, called sweethearts, are probably based on this original sugar-making material?

Tidbits 199

— By Xiong Yu

A very foolish person will not know what worries and anxieties there are in the world, but unfortunately I don't seem to be a very foolish person; a very wise person will not feel any worries and anxieties in the world either, but unfortunately I am not a very wise person either; in this way, I am often inevitably worried.

I remember that a certain staff member of the former Qing Dynasty said, "Heaven created our generation, neither making us wise, nor making us foolish, but giving us a body that is neither foolish nor wise, and placing us in a place that is neither dead nor alive"! Unfortunately, our encounters are mostly similar to this.

Mr. Zhang Ruogu, a writer familiar to readers of Spring and Autumn Magazine, has recently returned to China from Europe. In his spare time from writing, he is willing to serve as a French and piano professor for consulates or private individuals. Mr. Zhang has a deep understanding of the French language and is also proficient in music, so I am happy to introduce him. If there are any young people in this port who want to study with Mr. Zhang, please send a letter to Mr. Huang Jiping of the editorial department of this magazine for forwarding.

Records of Floating Fragrance 200

— Original by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

She said, "Hundreds of years ago, we Manchus were still a very small tribe! But the leader at that time had a very great spirit of courage and bravery. He could not be satisfied with the life of a chieftain, so he carefully planned to annex many nearby tribes together to form a strong and prosperous country. He first immersed himself in hard work, actively preparing; later, he saw that the time had come, and he resolutely launched an attack. But the nearby tribes were not willing to bow their heads and surrender for a while; therefore, fierce warfare began. The blood and heads of warriors were constantly flowing and being thrown on the battlefield; and each victory always belonged to us. Seeing our land gradually expand, our power also gradually increased. Unexpectedly, in a certain expedition, this capable and experienced leader fell into the enemy's trick, causing him and a small group of soldiers to be surrounded in a forest as large as this. The situation was indeed extremely dangerous; it was not known when the reinforcements would arrive, and the enemy's encirclement was increasing layer by layer, but he was not afraid at all and never prepared to surrender; he was determined to continue fighting, so that even if there was only the last soldier left, he would still have to fight. But on this day, his food was almost gone, and everyone could only eat the remaining cold rice, mixed with some wild vegetables. The next day, he was finally rescued. Later, in order to commemorate the brave, hardworking, and indomitable spirit of their ancestors, every generation of our rulers had to hold a special ceremony on this day; this ceremony was very simple, only needing to eat some cold rice rolled up with undercooked Shandong kelp." Saying this, she gestured to Li Lianying, who hurriedly sent a group of little eunuchs to bring several very large food boxes. (227)

World News

Parisian Theater Talk 201

— Mustard Seed

How many theaters are there in Paris? This is not an easy question to answer. In terms of large-scale theaters, there are probably over a hundred. The Opéra Garnier, which specializes in opera, and the Comédie-Française, which specializes in drama, are national theaters. As for privately established theaters, some perform opera, some perform drama, and some perform both opera and drama. There are so many different kinds that it is impossible to describe them all.

The architectural facilities of the national theaters are extremely magnificent. The plays performed there are all works of famous playwrights, and the actors are all the most famous in France. Sojourners living in Paris, when they find themselves in these national theaters, listening to singing and watching dancing, truly have the feeling that "this music should only exist in heaven, how often can it be heard in the human world!"

Here, we can certainly see the French nature of loving prosperity, but at the same time, we can also see the French adherence to old habits. The buildings of the various national theaters are all hundreds of years old. The carvings on the roofs and corridors are covered in cobwebs and dust, their splendor diminished. Some even display old stage curtains from the sixteenth century on the stage to show their long history.

The Comédie-Française, which performs dramas, also displays many statues of playwrights, all precious items from before the nineteenth century, such as Corneille, Molière, Hugo, and other statues of domestic and foreign playwrights. Among them, there is a statue of Fierre, which once had a wealthy nobleman willing to donate one million francs to purchase it but was unable to do so, which shows the value of those statues.

As for the privately established theaters, their architecture and facilities are newer than the national theaters. In particular, the plays and sets they perform are not as rigidly adhering to old conventions as the national theaters, so gentlemen who like fresh novelties flock to them.

In addition to theaters, there are also so-called music halls, which perform musical theater. Among them, one called the Moulin Rouge has stage settings, actors' costumes, lighting coordination, and the beauty of the music that surpasses other music halls. When we are among them, we can truly forget all the worries of life, as if entering a palace of pleasure.

The seat prices in music halls are several times higher than in ordinary theaters, and ordinary people do not dare to inquire. Most of the actors there engage in the life of goddesses, and ordinary families are even more reluctant to go. Those who linger there are wealthy merchants, foreigners, and young men who indulge in pleasure.

Paris's movie theaters are also scattered throughout the city, and the films shown are all from Hollywood. French-made films are only shown in smaller, less expensive movie theaters. In addition, there are also concert halls, circuses, vaudeville, and other theaters. Although there are not many, they still have their characteristics, which depend on the tastes of the people who go to the theaters.

The seat prices of the various theaters in Paris are determined by their position, front and back, high and low, expensive and cheap. Approximately the cheapest costs three or four francs (equivalent to about one yuan and five jiao in our currency), while the most expensive is more than seventy francs. The most expensive music halls can reach two or three hundred francs. A night of pleasure is worth the wealth of an average person. Prosperous Paris, extravagant Paris! Comparing it to Shanghai, the "Paris of the East," is truly far behind! —

Review of the Official Lineup 203

The Shanghai-Hong Kong interport football match is scheduled to be held in Hong Kong on February 4. The selection of the official players for the Shanghai team is a matter of utmost urgency. Goalkeepers Available 204

There are three players who have hopes of being selected for the goalkeeper position: Di Quli, Hua Te, and Shi Mitun. Each of the three players appeared once in the two trial matches. Di Quli conceded six goals, Hua Te conceded four goals, and Shi Mitun conceded eight goals. The number of goals conceded varies, and the circumstances are also different. Shi Mitun spent his career in the midst of wind and rain. Eight goals is undoubtedly a large number, but without his saves, it would have been even more than this number. The loss of these eight goals was truly beyond human ability. As for Di Quli and Hua Te, they also gave excellent performances yesterday. Hua Te's situation was even more dangerous than Di Quli's. The first two goals were caused by Jiang's missed kicks, the third goal was lost due to Ma Shaner's oversight, and the fourth goal was lost in the crowd. Overall, there was no chance to take advantage of. Of Di Quli's six goals, the first, second, fourth, and sixth goals were either very close range or accidental, and he was not to blame for the loss. As for the remaining third and fifth goals, there is much to discuss, and it is not necessarily the case that they could not have been saved. As for Ke Kelan, he is also one of the upcoming players, but due to his qualifications, comparing the four, Shi Mitun's official selection and Hua Te's backup should not be a big problem.

Ordinary Inner Guards 205

The inner guard positions include the Li Xiaoning and Lin Tuo group, the Ma Shaner and Shi Duke group, and the Ma Shaner and Jiang Shanjing group. The first group played in both matches. The Li Ning and Xiu Tuo group performed better the first time than the second time. Personally, Li Ning has a wealth of experience and has become more robust in his head and feet. His selection is undoubtedly. He is also a suitable assistant to Xiu Tuo. They have not been working together for long, so there are bound to be misunderstandings and confusion. However, if Ma Shaner is taken to replace Xiu Tuo, it will ultimately feel like the general is old and at the end of his strength. It is better to have someone who is young, strong, and able to fight for a long time. Jiang Shanjing is indeed a fierce general among the defenders, but his weakness is impatience. A little carelessness can lead to big mistakes. In conclusion, apart from Li Ning and Xiu Tuo, there are few competitors.

The center back position is the most difficult to select. Ga Xu is old, Gu Sitan has retired, and Pike is fat. So far, the outstanding players are Feng Yunyou, Chen Zhenxiang, and Xue Mengsi. He still needs to go through considerable military life.

Record of Cultural Construction Symposium 224

Liu Zhanen, Ou Yuanhuai and others all expressed their opinions.

Ten professors who signed the "Ten Declarations" held the first cultural construction symposium at the Central Society on Weihaiwei Road in this city at 5 pm on the 19th of this month. About 30 people attended. They took their seats at 5 pm and began talking at 6 pm. The meeting ended at 9 pm. All the attendees expressed brief and insightful opinions. Those who spoke knew everything and said everything, and those who listened listened attentively with open minds. The hosts and guests had extremely pleasant feelings. The contents of the meeting and symposium were recorded by stenographers from Bingxun Stenography Agency and the Chinese Stenography Society. Half of them took Chinese records, and half of them were translators. In a short time, a huge volume was obtained, which will be disclosed in the future, and there will be a grand view. The following is a brief record of the situation on that day:

Attendees: From the ten professors' side, He Bingsong, Zhen Xinyong, Sun Hanbing, Fan Zhongyun, Zhang Yi, and Wang Xinming attended. The guests were Liu Zhanen, Shu Xincheng, Shen Yinmo, Jin Tongyin, Huang Renzhi, Li Haoran, Zhu Xinong, Ni Wenzhou, Li Zhaohuan, Wu Lifu, Li Maimai, Ye Qing, Fu Donghua, Tao Baichuan, Tai Shuangqiu, Zhang Sumin, Wu Zijing, He Xiya, Shi Guogang, Yu Songhua, Xie Jiagan, Ou Yuanhuai, and Yu Chenghuan.

Report on the progress: The ten professors elected He Bingsong as chairman. He immediately stood up and reported on the progress of the declaration and the work that he wanted to do in the future. He hoped that the cultural pioneers attending the meeting would express their unique opinions and give strong guidance. Finally, he also reported on the criticisms of the "Ten Declarations" by the opinion circles in Shanghai, Nanjing, Beiping, and Hangzhou. After the report, he invited the guests to express their opinions.

Symposium situation: Many guests expressed their opinions that day. The main points are summarized as follows: (1) Liu Zhanen said that the words "China is gone" in the declaration are inevitably pessimistic. It must be known that a nation without self-confidence will perish, and there is no room for this pessimism. (2) Ou Yuanhuai said that China's culture today is a culture that is neither Chinese nor Western. In the future, the three transformations should be the highest principles, that is, the principles of scientification, standardization, and generalization. (3) Shen Yinmo said that he agreed with all the principles of the Ten Declarations, but how to make them concrete is the biggest problem. He hoped that the ten professors and the Chinese people would work hard on this in the future. (4) Yu Chenghuan said that the construction of China's local culture should be based on the countryside in order to be worthy of the name. (5) Jin Tongyin said that the first paragraph of the declaration is a diagnosis of China's diseases, the second paragraph describes the progress of treatment, and the third paragraph indicates the direction of future treatment. Now, I sincerely hope that the ten professors and those engaged in cultural undertakings can follow this direction and do some work of prescribing the right medicine. (6) Ni Wenzhou said that although the Ten Declarations only have abstract theories, they are a very effective medicine in opposing the inferiority complex of blindly following Western culture and discarding the exaggeration of clinging to the old feudal culture of China. At least it also has the value of psychological self-healing in medicine. (7) Shi Guogang said that cultural construction is not a matter for a few people, and the masses of cultural workers should be responsible for it together. (8) Li Zhaohuan said that China lacks the spirit of science the most, so the future cultural construction should be based on scientification as a prerequisite. (9) Ye Qing said that the Ten Declarations recognize that the needs of this time and place are the foundation of China's local culture. This is an attempt to make modern China truly modern. This attempt is to demand the modernization of China. (10) Fu Donghua said that it is useless to only talk about principles. After setting the principles, we must come up with concrete plans and be able to implement concrete methods in order to be useful. (11) Huang Renzhi said that to build a China-based culture, we should study the content of Chinese culture, analyze it carefully, and then determine the direction of taking and giving. (12) Li Haoran said that to solve the problem of China's cultural construction, we must first seek the balanced development of cities and villages, and education should not be exclusively for the rich. In today's villages and the poor being excluded from cultural life, we should pay attention to the issue of balanced development. (13) Zhu Yinong said that the three words "not sticking to the old" are inappropriate. I am against completely not sticking to the old. It should be "not clinging to the ancients." (14) Tao Baichuan said that the "not sticking to the old" in the declaration does have problems. As for "not blindly following," although it is an unbreakable principle, there must be concrete expressions in order to avoid the disease of superficiality. If the ten professors can have a supplementary and concrete declaration to show people the highest guiding principles, that would be the best thing. In addition, I advocate taking the Three People's Principles as the highest principle of cultural construction, and not adopting the experimental approach, because China's country and nation have been sacrificed by many erroneous experiments. The melon of Huangtai cannot be picked again and again, and no more erroneous experiments are allowed. (15) Tai Shuangqiu said that it is not known what the "needs of this time and place" referred to in the declaration are, but I think there are the needs of the majority and the needs of the minority, urgent needs and non-urgent needs. Cultural activists should take the urgent needs of the majority as needs. According to this view, cultural construction should be based on the Principle of People's Livelihood and aimed at national rejuvenation. (16) Zhang Sumin said that we should climb high from low and travel far from near. Now we should start with ourselves and spread to the masses to create a trend of the times. I not only hope that China has a local culture, but also hope that this local culture can be exported overseas. (17) Wu Lifu said that the theory of the Ten Declarations is beautiful, but we hope that this declaration is not just a theory of flowery language, but a plan to solve practical problems. (18) He Xiya said that I hope to have three points. The first point is to get rid of the three kinds of cowardly, conservative, and submissive psychology of fearing foreign culture, complaining about foreign culture, and blindly worshiping foreign culture. The first point is to take saving the nation as the prerequisite and backbone of cultural construction. The third point is that we must take the realization of the Three People's Principles in politics as the leading principle in politics and economy, promote the New Life Movement as the leading principle in social life, and pursue and create academic experience, knowledge, and skills that adapt to the times and national conditions as the leadership of thought, so that the three forces can be combined into one. Then we can nurture a brand-new Chinese local culture, that is, then we can make the Chinese people of the future both modern Chinese and not forget that they are Chinese people in the present world. (19) Li Maimai said that we should accept Europeanization and affirmatively declare the culture of capitalism. (20) Wu Zijing said that the biggest shortcoming of Chinese society is the lack of "obedience." I said that doing less empty talk and more practical things is also a shortcoming in China. Now we have two requirements: one is to require discipline, and the other is to require working hard in a down-to-earth manner. (21) Xie Yu said that cultural construction should be based on the Three People's Principles. The New Life Movement is a product of the Three People's Principles, and implementing the New Life Movement is a part of implementing the Three People's Principles. In addition, Yu Songhua made a written statement, which will not be repeated here.

Announcement of Adjournment 225

After everyone finished their statements, He Bingsong stood up to thank everyone, saying that we should accept everyone's sincere guidance, take the Three People's Principles as the highest principle of cultural construction, and announce that we will continue to hold similar symposiums in the future. All of your brilliant speeches will be recorded in the Cultural Construction Monthly without missing a word. It was already 9 pm, and the hosts and guests shook hands and dispersed.

Shenmei Girls' Middle School Increases the Number of Free Students 230

Shenmei Girls' Middle School on Baige Road in this city has always adhered to the sole purpose of sacrificing for education and working hard for society. In daily management, it is considered that true education is well managed, and it has long been deeply trusted by the general public. Recently, the school, in view of the economic downturn and the increasing number of students dropping out of school, decided to increase the number of free places in the primary and secondary school departments from the next semester, so that the children of poor families can have the opportunity to go to school. Once the news was announced, there was a rush to register and ask for information, and there was a problem of overcrowding. However, the school, based on its consistent spirit of sacrifice, decided to further expand the number of places, so that those who are ambitious can achieve their wishes. The school's enrollment period is set for January 25th. The classes are: three grades in the junior high school department, two classes in the national specialization department, one class in the elective women's weekday class, various grades in the elementary school department, and one class in kindergarten.

Current Status of the New Medical Community in Zhenhai 232

— Chen Zheyun

(1) County Territory Zhenhai is located in the eastern corner of Zhejiang Province, bordering the sea to the east, Cixi to the north, and Yin County to the southwest. Although the county area is not very large, it is listed as a second-class county because of its rich products. Also, because it is located at the mouth of the sea, it is a necessary route for seagoing ships to Ningbo, and it is the hub of the gateway to eastern Zhejiang. Therefore, a customs station is set up. Also, because of its strategic location, it is an important place for national defense and provincial defense. Therefore, gun emplacements are installed. This is the Hulang Pass that was formerly known, and today it is called Zhenhai Pass.

(2) Transportation The current transportation situation in this county has greatly improved compared with two years ago. Waterways have steamships, gasoline ships, and sailing ships. Since the construction of the highway, there are many roads for cars to gradually pass passenger cars. In addition, postal and telecommunications can reach major towns, so transportation is still convenient.

(3) New Medicine This county is located by the sea, and half of the people's occupations are fishing, half are agriculture, and the other half are business. Also, many people go out to do business, such as in Shanghai, Japan, Hong Kong, Singapore, and the three northeastern provinces. There are many patients with venereal diseases, which can be called the local disease of this county. The viruses are mostly brought from overseas. Whether in the city or in the towns, the public has a lot of faith in new medicine. But in the belief, there are still superstitions. For example, after being diagnosed and treated in the new medicine, the purchased and prepared medicines are offered to the gods and Buddhas, and after confessing and kneeling, they are taken. This kind of behavior is also common in the intellectual community. They call it co-medical treatment by humans and gods. Old medicine has no power in this county.

(4) Hygiene Because there are no professionals responsible for the administration of hygiene in this county, apart from the general official articles of writing in compliance with the order, they do not know its importance. Therefore, there are no achievements to be said in the city or in the towns. The so-called promotion of national health and public health, these points must be paid attention to.

(5) Hospitals In the city, there is one county hospital, one private Tongze Hospital, and several other private clinics. In the towns, there is one public Tongyi Hospital in Zhuangshi, one Lingyan Public Hospital in Lingyan Township, one public Tongan Hospital in Daqi, one private Lujiang Hospital in Chaiqiao, one private hospital in Xiaogang, one private Jintang Hospital in Jintang, and several other individual practitioners scattered in various towns. But there are no church hospitals. Among them, the equipment of Tongyi Hospital in Zhuangshi is the best. Second, there are Tongan Hospital in Daqi, Lingyan Public Hospital, Private Tongze Hospital, and County Hospital.

(6) Charitable Institutions (1) County Hospital (2) Daqi Tongan Hospital (3) Zhuangshi Tongyi Hospital (4) Lingyan Public Hospital. The above four hospitals are public, so they have a charitable nature. There is a free clinic for the poor and sick. Those who hold the hospital's free ticket will not be charged for medical expenses during outpatient hours. During the epidemic, the above four hospitals have temporary epidemic hospitals attached, but all have to charge for medicine. This is all due to financial reasons, so it is difficult to achieve good results. I should ask the major philanthropists of this county to donate more and generously help the above four hospitals.

(7) Doctor Level The qualifications of doctors practicing in this county can be roughly divided into three: (1) graduates from Zhejiang Provincial Medical College, (2) graduates from major hospitals, and (3) graduates from Shanghai Southeast Medical College. The total number of doctors in the county is about fifty or sixty. Doctors have good moral concepts, no factional divisions, and no advertising to attract patients.

(8) Obstetrics The public has a lot of faith in new medicine for delivery, but most of them go home immediately after giving birth in the hospital without staying. Among them, the above four charitable organizations charge lower fees, but there is no establishment of a civilian obstetrics department in this county, which is a disadvantage.

(9) New Medical Groups There are no formal organizations such as doctors' associations for new medicine in this county, and there is no publicity of new medical publications. Although Doctor Cheng Yuzhi and others formed the Zhenhai New Medical Association in the autumn of last year, its purpose was to request the Ministry of Health to set up a doctor's refresher course to recruit doctors who had not registered due to the expiration of the regulations for flexible issuance of certificates. It is not an academic group.

Chinese Medicine and Hygiene in the Past Year (3) 233

— Jiang Haiming

Introduction—Medical Education—Medical Group Activities—Medical Disputes—Medical Publishing—Medical Inspection—Medical Construction—Military Medical Training—A Glimpse of the Old Medical and Pharmaceutical Circles—New Pharmaceutical Industry Trends—Rural Health Survey—Urban Health View—Conclusion

(10) New Pharmaceutical Industry Trends

In the past year, the new pharmaceutical industry operated by Chinese people has developed considerably. Although it is difficult to compare with the products of foreign companies such as Qianxin, Lilli, Kongshi, Xianling, and Baowei in terms of manufacturing, it is still very satisfying. Among the domestic pharmaceutical factories, the fastest progress is made by Xinya. In the spring of the 23rd year, Qiangji Company was newly established in Hankou, specializing in promoting Xinya's proprietary Chinese medicines. The business volume is increasing day by day, and it has penetrated into the hinterland of Sichuan, Hunan, Henan, and Jiangxi, which is enough to resist a part of foreign goods and recover a lot of profit. Products such as Minyi, Minsheng, and Xinyi are also mostly excellent. Although the annual sales volume of each factory is not detailed, which is a great regret, it is expected that in this year of disaster and drought, it may exceed other production and sales products.

As for manufacturing, the trend of domestic pharmaceutical factories is to try to imitate foreign goods as much as possible. For example, the "Chang Li Jun Zhi" produced by Xinya in the summer is an oral preparation in ampoules, which can be said to be a novel creation in the production of new medicines in China.

Regarding the promotion of new drugs, it seems that foreign manufacturers are the most concerned. The methods are novel and meaningful, and there are endless new ideas. For example, the "Womunadin" essay contest held by Qianxin Company in mid-October has done its best to publicize. It is expected that domestic manufacturers may follow suit. However, the psychology of merchants liking counterfeiting has become a common problem. In recent years, there are still many new drug advertisements that ignore the facts and exaggerate the propaganda. Our health authorities need to pay active attention to it.

After the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, in the spring of the 23rd year, Russian medicines were once dumped in the Chinese market. To this day, many raw materials for medicines are still Russian goods, which is also worth noting.

(11) Rural Health Survey

The September issue of the Chinese Journal of Medicine and Pharmacy in the 23rd year published an article by Mr. Li Ting'an entitled "Investigation Report on Rural Health in China", which describes the situation of rural health in China in detail and shows his thoughts. Mr. Li completed this article with the cooperation of Mr. Yao Xunyuan of the Ministry of Health, so it is very serious. The investigators include:

Zhejiang Province - (1) Wuxing (2) Wukang and other County Hospitals

Guangdong Province - Guangzhou Family Promotion Association

According to the results of the survey, there are a total of seventeen places where rural health has been built in China. The lack of quantity is undoubtedly true; moreover, from the general situation obtained from the survey, there are about six impressions of its shortcomings:

First, the establishment has not been widespread. Second, the organization cannot be uniform. Third, it has not been long. Fourth, the funding is exhausted. Fifth, there is a lack of talent. Sixth, the work is monotonous, similar but not specialized. In a word, China's rural health cause is still in the experimental budding stage. Although the work in various places tends to focus on treatment and prevention, it is only because the establishment has not been widespread, and there are no good results to be said. Although, the Shanghai Gaoqiao Rural Health Model Experimental Zone and others have many good designs and performances, but they are only limited to one corner, so it goes without saying that our country's rural health is behind the Western countries. I can't help but deeply hope that my colleagues in the world and those responsible for health administration will actively seek the soundness of the rural health cause in order to seek universal development and determine the direction of future improvement.

The year with the most progress in the annual increase in the number of rural health agencies was the 22nd year of the Republic of China. In the 23rd year of the Republic of China, only one place was added. How slow is it? We feel the importance of the rural health cause, and we cannot ignore the increase in the "quantity" of rural health construction. Common Sense Q&A about Diseases 234

— Cheng Hanzhang

(51) Relapsing Fever (Part 2)

(Question) After the fever subsides in a bout of relapsing fever, when will the fever return?

(Answer) Typically, after the fever subsides once, a second bout of fever occurs after five to seven days.

(Question) What is the condition like at this time?

(Answer) At this time, it is similar to the first bout of fever, with chills, shivering, and high fever; however, the severity and duration are reduced.

(Question) When will these repeated bouts of fever stop?

(Answer) Relapsing fever usually stops after the second or third bout; occasionally, there are fourth or fifth bouts. However, in these cases, the intervals become longer, the duration of the bouts becomes shorter, and the fever is lower.

(Question) Based on what you said, the course of relapsing fever is usually regular; but I wonder if there are any abnormal courses?

(Answer) There are also abnormal courses; however, they are rare.

(Question) What are the abnormal courses of relapsing fever?

(Answer) The abnormal courses of relapsing fever include fewer bouts, shorter duration, and sudden cessation. Some resemble malaria-like attacks. Others involve nervous system symptoms, or jaundice, bleeding from the skin and mucous membranes, vomiting blood, and bloody diarrhea. This particular condition is called biliary relapsing fever.

(Question) Do patients with relapsing fever experience complications?

(Answer) Various complications can occur.

(Question) Which complications are most likely to occur during the course of relapsing fever?

(Answer) In addition to bronchitis and bronchopneumonia, splenic infarction or splenic abscess can occur. This can lead to peritonitis, which is very dangerous.

(Question) What other complications are there?

(Answer) There can also be persistent nosebleeds, glandular inflammation, dysentery-like ulcers, hemorrhagic nephritis, and iritis. However, circulatory disorders are rare.

(Question) When we encounter a patient with relapsing fever, how should we diagnose it?

(Answer) To diagnose relapsing fever, one should pay attention to the onset of the illness, whether it begins with chills and shivering and a rapid onset of fever, splenomegaly, and recurrence of fever. In addition, the pathogenic spirochetes can be examined in the blood.

Page 16

(Question) What is the prognosis of this disease, good or bad?

(Answer) Despite the severity of the symptoms in relapsing fever, the mortality rate is very low, only about two to four percent.

(Question) What is the treatment for relapsing fever?

(Answer) At the beginning of the fever period, Salvarsan or Neosalvarsan (commonly known as 606 and 914), which are arsenic preparations, can be injected. Because the pathogen is a spirochete, these types of drugs are highly effective.

(Question) How should we prevent the spread of this disease?

(Answer) Because this disease is spread by blood-sucking insects, prevention methods involve eliminating bedbugs, lice, fleas, etc.

The Three Principles of the People and Medicine 235

— Song Guobin

The Three Principles of the People are the only way to govern the country and bring peace to the world. Its essence is that it can be questioned by a hundred generations without doubt and will last for ten thousand years. There is no need for us to elaborate on this. What we want to talk about now is only about the medical aspect. In other words, it is the relationship between the Three Principles of the People and medicine.

(1) Nationalism

The meaning of the two words "nationalism" is too broad! On the surface, many revolutionary martyrs sacrificed countless blood, all for the revival of the nation. However, this goal has not been achieved to this day. How can the medical profession, being only one of a hundred professions, bear such a heavy responsibility? It must be known that this view is wrong. Although there is more than one way to revive the nation, the most fundamental and basic work must be undertaken by doctors. The ancients said in medical texts: "To strengthen a country, one must first strengthen its people." This saying has twelve points of profound truth. In other words, a healthy nation requires a healthy people. How can the people be healthy? This question cannot be solved with empty words; it must be done practically. The biggest enemy of health is disease. Therefore, the healthier a nation, the more diseases it has, and the higher the mortality rate. Why is this? It is simply because the people do not know about hygiene, so all kinds of infectious diseases follow one after another! When they are not sick, they have no preventative measures in place; and when they are sick, they often die needlessly because medical services are underdeveloped—such as insufficient distribution of doctors and too few hospitals. In this way, the nation naturally moves towards aging day by day! We only need to look at the advanced countries of the West. Isn't their level of civilization directly proportional to the health of their people? At the same time, aren't the development of their medical and hygiene undertakings directly proportional to their level of civilization and the health of their people? Understanding this point, one knows the relationship between medicine and the nation! Take our China, for example. The lack of vigor of the people can be said to have reached its extreme! But when one investigates the reasons, it is mostly due to disease and lack of hygiene. The widespread prevalence of pulmonary tuberculosis is an obvious proof of this. As a result, weak genes are passed down, becoming weaker and weaker. At this time, the method of remedy can only be undertaken by doctors. How can we prevent diseases and eliminate germs? How can we popularize hygiene knowledge? All of this depends on the work and publicity of doctors. Our colleagues! Quickly take on this responsibility of reviving the nation!

The aggression of imperialists is intensifying day by day! It can almost be said that they are penetrating every hole and drilling every gap. Taking our medical community as an example, this phenomenon is becoming more and more obvious. What about foreign doctors? Their influence in China is growing day by day. What about foreign medicine? It is extraordinarily filling the markets! But the latter only invades our country's billions of dollars every year. As for the former? That is truly extremely dangerous! Entrusting the lives of our people to those who are not of our race is extremely dangerous for the future of the nation! Our only important task at this time is how to eliminate the influence of foreign doctors in China, to save the lives of our people from the brink of danger, and at the same time, how to imitate foreign medicines, resist foreign imports, and recover the country's losses even if it is only a fraction. I think this work is crucial to the safety of the nation and the rights of the country!

(2) Civil Rights

As long as one carefully studies the definition of the two words "civil rights," one can know that civil rights are a kind of right that everyone has. However, because of the nature of the profession, there is often a special right in addition to ordinary civil rights. In practice, this right is also one of civil rights, but it only applies to people in one profession and is not universal! This right for doctors is called medical rights. The medical laws and regulations of various countries often stipulate the special rights that doctors should enjoy in great detail. Because without this, doctors will feel thorny in their professional work! Our country is not like this. Society cannot understand the rights that doctors should have, and the doctors themselves? They also often do not know that they should enjoy special rights in their profession. As a result, medical rights are robbed, and even ordinary civil rights are gradually eroded! Looking at the medical disputes in the past year or two, one can know. Patients can file illegal lawsuits, and government agencies can make illegal arrests and illegal imprisonments. Isn't this evidence that even ordinary civil rights have been eroded? In order to maintain professional safety and to break through the surrounding bad environment, we must not only safeguard our due civil rights, but also strive for our due medical rights. We must use the spirit of developing civil rights to develop medical rights, which is one of the civil rights. Isn't this very much in line with the late Premier's Doctrine of Civil Rights?

(3) People's Livelihood

The first element of people's livelihood is production, which no one can object to. The level of productivity is controlled by the working class, which seems to have nothing to do with doctors. However, after careful study, it is not only related, but it can be said that the amount of productivity is almost indirectly controlled by doctors. Why is this? Productivity is directly proportional to the size of the population. Countries with large populations often have sufficient productivity. To have a large population, the mortality rate must be reduced. To reduce the mortality rate, the people must have strong physiques. How to make the people's physiques strong and how to reduce the mortality rate, we must ask our doctors! Therefore, the medical profession has a direct relationship with the nation and an indirect relationship with the people's livelihood. And this indirect relationship is no less important than the direct relationship!

Based on the above three points, it can be known that the medical profession has a deep relationship with the late Premier's Three Principles of the People! Now that we understand the relationship between the Three Principles of the People and ourselves, we must further study how to develop the spirit of the Three Principles of the People and how to undertake this major basic work. I want to tell the people of society not to regard medicine as a minor path and despise it, and our colleagues should not regard themselves as a minor path and ignore our natural duties and the human rights we should enjoy!

Common Sense of Ear, Nose, Throat, and Eye Hygiene 236

— Tang Renjin

(32) Scarlet Fever (Continued)

Pathogen—In this era of flourishing medicine, everyone has recognized that scarlet fever is an acute rash-like infectious disease, the same as measles, rubella, smallpox, chickenpox, and other diseases. Unfortunately, its real cause is still unknown. Although some researchers have reported the pathogenic bacteria of this disease, it has not yet been truly recognized by the medical community. However, judging from the results of streptococcal serum treatment of scarlet fever, the theory that streptococcus is the pathogenic bacteria of this disease seems to be closer to the truth.

Infectiousness—The infectiousness of this disease is particularly strong, especially when there is fever and during the recovery period. The chance of infection does not necessarily have to be from the patient's clothes, bedding, books, toys, etc. Sometimes, it can be transmitted simply by being in the same room with the patient for a short while. Its virus is mostly present in the patient's tissues, body fluids, secretions, and excretions. Therefore, the patient's blood, tears, nasal mucus, sputum, urine, feces, epithelial desquamation (during the recovery period), etc., all have the ability to transmit the disease.

Age—Children around five years old are most susceptible to this disease. People in their teens to twenties are also often infected. If they are over forty years old, it is difficult to be infected.

Port of entry for the virus—Mostly from the pharyngeal tonsils (commonly known as palatine tonsils).

Season of epidemic—This disease can be epidemic in all seasons in large cities with dense populations. However, it is most prevalent in autumn and winter.

Incubation period of scarlet fever—Approximately four to eight days. However, there are times when it is as short as one day or as long as two weeks.

Prodromal period of scarlet fever—The prodromal period of this disease is characterized by chills, shivering, fever, headache, nausea, vomiting, lethargy, sore throat, and difficulty swallowing. At this time, the body temperature is mostly as high as 39 or 40 degrees Celsius.

Scarlet fever rash—The rash begins to appear the day after the prodromal period occurs, which is when the body temperature rises to its highest point. The skin rash that occurs in this disease has very unique characteristics compared to the skin rash that occurs in other acute rash-like infectious diseases. The rash is initially small, bright red spots that are densely distributed on the surface of the skin. These spots spread very quickly, so they can soon interconnect and merge into patches.
